Not as painful as the other stuff I tried and so much more effective. And I did not get purple marks from burst blood vessels which happened with all the other methods. And the redness went away amazingly fast.  Not messy.  Cleans up with warm water.     <li> Let me start off by saying that I am very fair skinned, I bruise very easily, and I have very thick dark hair. I am unable to use hot wax for hair removal due to extremely sensitive skin, which I found out the hard way after getting waxed (with what the woman said was for sensitive skin). I have been plucking, shaving, and bleaching to remove or lighten various unwanted hair. Those methods are fine for most areas, but far from ideal for for others. I used to dread swimsuit season for obvious reasons, so when I came across Moom I decided to give it a go after some research. I read all the instructions thoroughly before my 1st use... I&#x27;m not sure exactly where things went wrong, but I ended up with some bruising, bleeding from the hair follicles, and to add insult to injury, it only removed 3/4 of the hair, so I had to pluck the strays. It did hurt, but anything that rips your hair out at the root is going to hurt to some degree. Despite the bruising and bleeding, it honestly wasn&#x27;t as painful as I expected... I should note that if I accidentally pluck a hair that is too far into my eyebrows I bleed as well, and hot wax made my eyebrows red and swollen for a week.     I decided to give sugaring another chance, because I knew I was doing something wrong, the hair that was removed took 3 weeks to grow back, and once the bruising went away  a couple of days later there weren&#x27;t any ingrown hairs. The 2nd time around I watched several you tube videos, and decided to try the traditional flicking technique instead of the applicator and strips. The results were about the same, only more messy. It took about 4 weeks for the hair to grow back, but this time I noticed it grew back finer.     My first 2 attempts were definitely user error, and apparently hair that had been previously shaved is extremely stubborn. 3rd time is a charm, right? I watched the Moom video on you tube, and used the technique that Moom outlines in the instructions, and in the video. I can&#x27;t stress enoughthat when applying the sugar, the sugar absolutely must be proper consistency, paper thin, and in the correct direction, otherwise it doesn&#x27;t grab the hair properly. My persistence paid off... 3rd time IS a charm... NO bruising, and NO hair! There was still some bleeding from some follicles, but only in the spots that I had missed previously. I expect there won&#x27;t be bleeding next time around if the trend is consistent.     Verdict:  I gave Moom only 4 stars because the learning curve is a little painful, and I feel the instructions could be a bit better, but the video was definitely helpful. I highly recommend watching it before you start. I also feel that they should have included plastic applicators instead of wooden tongue depressors. I really like that it&#x27;s all natural, and it&#x27;s not as harsh as hot wax. I can simply wash it off with water if I accidentally get some on a spot that I didn&#x27;t intend to, and I need only wash the muslin strips and they are ready to reuse for the next use. I&#x27;m extremely happy with the product, and the results.</li>

Cons  -Like all hair removal products, it misses hair sometimes. But unlike wax, you can go back over with Moom instead of using tweezers.  -Ok, I really can&#x27;t think of anything else.    A couple tips:  -If you decide to warm up the wax by letting it float in hot water, make sure to put the Moom jar in the container, then fill the container up with water. I did the opposite (I put water in a bowl, then dropped the Moom jar in), and water got in the jar. Because Moom is made out of sugar, the water liquefied a chunk of Moom. I poured out the water and destroyed Moom from the jar, but we&#x27;ll see if it still works in the next couple of month.  -If you&#x27;re waxing sensitive areas for the first time (like the bikini area), use the small strips designated for your eyebrows/lip/chin.   -Make sure you pull the cloth as parallel to your skin as possible. It hurts less. Make sure you hold your skin taunt too, because it also reduces the pain.    I usually don&#x27;t write long reviews, but Moom is definitely the way to go! Forget the hard and soft waxes - they just hurt! Trust me, if you&#x27;re waxing for the first time, especially in the bikini area, choose Moom!!</li>

    <li> this product works really well if you use it properly. i bought it to use on my bikini area but it works on finer facial hair as well. here are some tips for using the product:    * make sure you&#x27;re hair is in the right length range - 1/4\\&quot; to 1/2\\&quot; works best in my experience. if the hair is too long or short the product won&#x27;t work. you can buy a beard/bikini trimmer to uniformly trim the hair to the right length.  * wash the area before waxing (any lotions, natural oils, etc will interfere with the ability of the product to stick to the hair)  * thoroughly dry the area before waxing and if necessary, keep a tissue with you to wipe off areas that may get wet/damp again (like underarms)   * the wax consistency should be fluid, but don&#x27;t overheat so it&#x27;s like water  * apply a thin coat - There&#x27;s usually smaller, finer hairs remaining after a first wax.&lt;br /&gt;- Make sure your skin is lotion-free and completely dry before beginning&lt;br /&gt;- Make sure the product is heated hot enough (obviously don&#x27;t burn yourself, but I get it pretty hot). I&#x27;ve found it works much much better when it&#x27;s a more liquid-like consistency and you can spread it on really thin. You do NOT need a lot of the stuff. Be sure to brush on the wax with the hair growth direction and peel back against hair growth - it&#x27;s not a straight up pull where you&#x27;re ripping your skin upward, it&#x27;s more of a fast peel action in the opposite direction of the hair growth.&lt;br /&gt;- Don&#x27;t expect to be magically hair free the first time. Also, it takes a LONG time to do this. Particularly with the Moom because they don&#x27;t give you enough strips or Moom stuff to do it all at once.     <li> Hi, I wanted to share what I thought was a better way to use this product to get results you want.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;  Background: I&#x27;m Middle Eastern originally, and have been using sugar wax most of my life to remove hair, however it&#x27;s always easier when someone does the waxing for you, as when you do it alone it can be very messy. But I was fed up of spending so much money on getting waxed and I decided to do it myself.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Usually sugar wax is used at room temperature when you just want to do basic spreading and pulling (it&#x27;s a technique you have to learn through observation, then trial and error).&lt;br /&gt;But I liked Moom&#x27;s idea of using a couple of extra tools ( spreading stick and cloths) to get the job done with less agony. And after a couple of sessions here and there, and much experience generally with sugar wax, I can say this is my favorite way to use this product:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- Do not heat the wax in the Microwave as suggested by Moom, for centuries people have used sugar wax at room temperature. And I find this is best...as even when slightly heated it gets too sticky and cannot grab the hair as firmly. When at room temperature the wax can get a firmer grip of the hair without going all over the place in a messy way ( and hence is not as painful when pulling).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- As opposed to spreading the wax on the hair directly (which I find can be messy and painful sometimes when the hair is slightly long), instead spread a thin layer of the wax on the cloth itself, making sure you have an area relative to that you&#x27;re targeting on your body. So for bikini line, I&#x27;ll spread a thin layer on the cloth, that is long and somewhat wide. I&#x27;ve used the smaller cloths for smaller areas. Note: it&#x27;s more manageable to spread thin layer of wax on the cloth than it is on your body, especially for smaller, more sensitive areas.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- When you put the waxed cloth on the body part your targeting, just tap and rub it a few times gently, making sure its in place, that also slightly warms the wax. Then wait for like 2-3 seconds (gives time for the sugar to settle) and pull with a quick firm grip.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So that&#x27;s basically my favorite way of using this product, less messiness, less product wasting (for both the sugar and the cloths) and MUCH less pain.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Hope this helps &#x3D;)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Side Note: Btw I only use this for my bikini area (the whole area) and sometimes under arms, for everything else I use an epilator machine.lso slightly warms the wax. You definitely do have to go over most areas more than once, especially if your hairs grow in pretty random directions and not in much of a \\&quot;pattern\\&quot; like mine.  It&#x27;s very specific to the direction of your growth, if that makes any sense, more so than regular wax. I was disappointed to find out after my first session that I still ended up with the unsightly whiteheads the next day (and of course a few more in the days to follow).  So I hit the internet up and came across a recipe for homemade Tend Skin - just search for it and you can make some too.  I used it on my existing zits and they seemed to go away faster and I didn&#x27;t see any new ones.  I also came across some other promising things I could try my next time MOOMing.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So this most recent session, I washed my face in warm water (to loosen up the pores and their grip on the hairs) and mild Dove soap first.  I swabbed the area with a little alcohol first, and when this dried, applied a light dusting of powder so the MOOM would stick better. And when I used the MOOM, I applied AGAINST the hair growth (and rubbed on the cloth strip against the growth), and removed in the SAME direction as growth.  Some websites I had visited stated that this was the correct way to do sugaring, and MOOM is really just a form of sugaring.  I found that it removed the hair as well or betterthan last time, and it felt slightly gentler and less painful this way.  I did small patches at time, also trying to let areas rest a bit before going back over them.  After MOOMing, I washed the area again with COLD water (to close those infection-prone pores) and the same mild soap, dried the area, and applied the home-made Tend Skin solution (really just crushed up Asprin, witch hazel and alcohol).  I am also planning on not touching the area at all, as I know this can contribute to pimples.  It looks great this time, with minimal redness and almost no stray hairs, and feels clean and cool.  I will keep my fingers crossed that no whiteheads come in - I have a good feeling about it though, I have to say!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Oh, and it goes without saying that the cleanup with this stuff is waaaay easier than with wax, since it is water soluble. The wax also wipes off really well with some warm water, so it was easy to clean my body, hands, sticks, and strips for next time.     <li> As someone who has been waxing my own legs for a couple of years, MOOM was easy and effective.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Tips for the best hair follicle ripping experience:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1. Ensure hair is 1/4&amp;#34; - 1/2&amp;#34; long otherwise lots of hairs will get left behind.  Too short, and they wont get picked up.. too long and it&#x27;ll just be a gross painful mess.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1. Of course test this on your skin first - if you&#x27;re sensitive to heat wait a bit longer.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;4. Spread wax thinly - spread the wax very thinly in the direction of hair growth.  You want there to be a very thin and shiny coat, but not have it globby or streaky.  Then immediately put the strip on, firmly press down in the direction of hair growth a couple times.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;5.
